class="asset-double-wide double-wide p402_premium" role="main" itemprop="articleBody"><div id="module-position-O0B0f5e3Wco" class="story-asset story-metadata-asset"><div data-mycapture-sm-src="http://cdn.tegna-tv.com/-mm-/09da95c722267d39482739d3d9a574c015571d4c/r=360x400/local/-/media/2016/02/08/WXIA/WXIA/635905278016955978-Otis.JPG" /><span class="story-asset inline-share-tools-asset"><div class="inline-share-tools asset-inline-share-tools asset-inline-share-tools-top"><span

        class="inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-linkedin"
        data-share-method="linkedin"

        href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?url=http%3A//on.11alive.com/1T8OsHI&amp;mini=true"
        target="_blank" data-popup
                ><span class="inline-share-count inline-share-count-linkedin"></span><span class="inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-linkedin">LINKEDIN</span></a><span
            class="inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-comments"
            data-share-method="comments"
            data-uotrack="InlineShareCommentsBtn"><span class="inline-share-count inline-share-count-comments">
                1
            </span><span class="inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-comments">COMMENT</span></span><span
        class="inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-email"
        data-share-method="email"
        data-uotrack="InlineShareEmailBtn"><span class="inline-share-count inline-share-count-email"></span><span class="inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-email">EMAIL</span></span><span
         class="inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-more"
         data-share-method="facebook"
         data-uotrack="InlineShareMoreBtn"><span class="inline-share-count inline-share-count-more"></span><span class="inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-more">MORE</span></span></div></div><p>ATLANTA -- A mancharged withthe murder of a 75-year-oldwomancould be on the verge of freedomdue to a mistake made by the judge presiding over the case.</p><p>On Monday, the Supreme Court of Georgia announced Geary Otiscouldnotbe prosecuted for the murder 2013 murder of Mary Oliver due todouble jeopardy.</p><p>Otis' public defender, Amanda Grantham, went to tell him the news just hours after the unanimous ruling was released.</p><p>"I think at first he was kind of stunned, and didn't know what to say because it was kind of sudden," said Bryan Grantham, Amanda's husband and Otis' co-counsel.</p><p>Otis was 64 years oldwhen police say he racedup a set of stairs at theBaptist Towerswhere he and Oliver lived. He allegedly fought withEmmanuel Surry, who was taken to Grady Memorial Hospital, before kicking in the door to Oliver's room and stabbing her several times. Evidence showed Oliver was stabbed with such force that itcutinto her bone and spinal column.</p><p>Police found Otis covered in blood and carrying two large kitchen knives.He hadto be subdued by Tasers.</p><p>At his trial, Otis' attorney AmandaGranthamasked the court to consider "what crazy people look like," as "mental illness" comes in many forms."I'll be asking for the only verdict that speaks the truth in this case, and that Geary is not guilty by reason of insanity."</p><p>Prosecutors immediately called foul, arguing that was the first time they were told the defense would be using insanity as an argument.They asked for a continuance, a few days to research Otis' mental health.</p><p>If Judge Ural Glanville had agreed, the trial would have continued as allowed by law. But instead, Glanvilledeclared a mistrial.The Supreme Court saidthat was mistake, because any new trial now would amount to double jeopardy,trying Otis twice for the same crime.</p><p>Bryan Grantham understands some people might be frustrated by the Supreme Court's decision but argues,"If you're going to celebrate America,you have to celebrate that when errors are made in the legal system,part of the justice is that we don't tolerate that."</p><p>Oliver's family did not respond to our calls.</p><p>"The probably don't like us very much right now and I can understand that. But at the end of the day we're not just defending Geary Otis, we're defending a system," said Grantham when asked what he would say to Oliver's family, who will now never get a chance to hold the man they believe killed her accountable.</p><p>Glanville also said he could not comment at this time. If the decision holds, he will have to sign the paper officially setting Otis free.</p><p>Fulton County District Attorney Paul Howard said in a statement that his office is filing an appeal. The statement read:</p><div><p></p><blockquote><p>In the matter of <u>Geary Otis v. The State</u>, Fulton County District Attorney Paul L. Howard Jr. states that this case involves the brutal home invasion and stabbing death of 76-year-old retiree, Mary Oliver. Mrs. Oliver, who had just returned from a birthday celebration with her daughter, was stabbed multiple times throughout her head and body. Additionally, the defendant assaulted a male retiree and an Atlanta Police Officer at the same complex with the knife used to murder Mrs. Oliver.</p><p>To hold that the State cannot try the Defendant because a Fulton County Judge declared a mistrial under the circumstances of this case is shocking to the consciousness of justice and fair play. Particularly, when we consider the courts concurrent opinion written by Supreme Justice David Nahmias.</p><p>Justice Nahmias said, It is apparent that the trial court in this case was striving to reach a fair trial.</p><p>Such an outcome is beyond belief. We are filing an immediate request for reconsideration.</p></blockquote></div><div id="module-position-O0B0f5hanHA" class="story-asset image-asset"><aside itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" class="single-photo float"><img itemprop="url" src="http://cdn.tegna-tv.com/-mm-/6e4a7d28533569b1f8b5b553f6ce993ee73b377c/c=4-0-341-449&amp;r=183&amp;c=0-0-180-240/local/-/media/2016/02/08/WXIA/WXIA/635905301480904794-oliver.JPG" alt="Mary Oliver" width="180" height="240" data-mycapture-src=""
                    data-mycapture-sm-src="" /><meta itemprop="name" content="635905301480904794-oliver.JPG" /><meta itemprop="height" content="240" /><meta itemprop="width" content="180" /><p>Mary Oliver<meta itemprop="copyrightHolder" content="11Alive" />&nbsp;<span class="credit">(Photo: 11Alive)</span></p></aside></div><p>Oliver's family <a href="/story/news/local/2014/03/05/1939720/">filed a lawsuit against Baptist Towers Apartments</a> shortly after the murder.Her daughters accused the facility's security of being noticeably lax over atwoyear span-- <a href="/news/article/297538/40/Prostitution-drugs-and-murder-alleged-at-senior-center">allowing some residents to buy drugs and hire prostitutes</a>.</p><p>Otis, who was facing life in prison without parole, currently remains at the Fulton County Jail. Grantham says it will likely be several weeks before he is released.</p><p><strong>RELATED | More mug shots</strong></p><div id="module-position-O0B0f5guZ9U" class="story-asset gallery-asset"><div class="galleries embedded_story hasendslate clearfix"
